# DUAL INDEPENDENT AUDIT — I-meta-008 #1034 (prefer clean abstract over non-deterministic OA scrape)

You are one of TWO independent auditors (Claude + Codex) running in PARALLEL (§-1.1). This is
a DESIGN-DECISION review as well as a code review — scrutinize the decision, not just the syntax.

## LIVE GROUND TRUTH (verified this session, deployed path, DOI 10.1257/jep.33.2.3 = Acemoglu
"Automation and New Tasks", the canonical paper that read "not extractable" in run 6)

Three repeated fetches of the SAME entity returned THREE different `oa_full_text` values:
1. 25,000-char **Sci-Hub HTML** page (`<!DOCTYPE html> ... <title>Sci-Hub. Automation...`).
2. 25,000-char **Jina landing-page markdown** (`Title: Automation... Markdown Content: Jo...`).
3. Clean **1,331-char CrossRef abstract** (`We present a framework for understanding...`).

So the OA scrape is NON-DETERMINISTIC and junk-prone, while the abstract is clean + stable.
The earlier thin-stub fix (length >= 1200 → "real full text") could NOT catch the 25K Sci-Hub
HTML (it passes any length check) → generator got 25K of HTML → "not extractable".

After this fix, with PG_FRAME_PREFER_ABSTRACT=1, Acemoglu grounds DETERMINISTICALLY across 3
repeated live fetches: quote_source=crossref_abstract, 1331 chars, clean prose, identical each time.

## The change
1. `_looks_like_html_junk(text)` — head contains `<!doctype`/`<html`/`<head`/`<body`/`sci-hub` → junk.
2. `_is_usable_full_text(text)` — usable only if `len >= _OA_FULLTEXT_MIN_CHARS (1200)` AND NOT junk.
   Used in Step 4 OpenAlex gate + the decision `real_full_text`.
3. `_FRAME_PREFER_ABSTRACT` (env `PG_FRAME_PREFER_ABSTRACT`, default OFF). When ON: the decision
   prefers the clean abstract (CrossRef/OpenAlex/PubMed) over a scraped full text; Step 4 also
   fetches OpenAlex even when a usable full text exists (so the abstract is available to prefer).
4. `run_gate_b.py` sets `PG_FRAME_PREFER_ABSTRACT=1` + `PG_OPENALEX_FRAME_FALLBACK=1` via setdefault.
5. Default OFF preserves the M-66b-T clinical full-text path (trial 9-field rosters live in tables,
   not abstracts); existing M-66b-T tests stay green (full_text ~1650 clean → still oa_full_text).

Diff: `.codex/I-meta-008-htmljunk/codex_diff.patch`. Full file: `src/polaris_graph/retrieval/frame_fetcher.py`.

## Audit questions (independent, line-by-line)
1. **Is preferring the abstract the RIGHT design** for frame-contract grounding, given the scrape's
   proven non-determinism? Or does it lose important content vs a clean full text? Consider that the
   contract required_fields for these entities are abstract-level (thesis/mechanism/displacement_vs_
   reinstatement/empirical_support). Is the OFF-by-default + run_gate_b-ON gating correct (no clinical
   regression)?
2. **Determinism**: is the fix deterministic under the flag? (Abstract source is CrossRef→OpenAlex,
   both deterministic; scrape is bypassed.) `_pick_richest_abstract` tie-handling.
3. **`_looks_like_html_junk` robustness**: false positives (a real abstract that happens to contain
   "<html>" or the word "sci-hub")? false negatives (other junk shapes)? Is head-only (600 chars) right?
4. **`_is_usable_full_text` + the flag interaction** in Step 4 and the decision — any path where a
   junk scrape still becomes direct_quote, or a real full text is wrongly dropped?
5. **Regression**: M-66b-T (flag off) unchanged? The provenance labels (OPEN_ACCESS vs ABSTRACT_ONLY)
   correct under the new prefer-abstract branch?
6. **Sci-Hub**: the access layer pulled content from Sci-Hub. Flag the legal/provenance severity for a
   clinical product (is rejecting it in frame_fetcher enough, or does the access_bypass Sci-Hub method
   itself need gating? — note as a finding; out of scope for THIS diff to fully fix).

+def _looks_like_html_junk(text: str) -> bool:
+    """True when a fetched 'full text' is actually raw HTML markup or a
+    Sci-Hub wrapper page rather than clean extracted prose (#1034
+    follow-up). Ground-truthed: aeaweb paywalled econ papers (e.g.
+    Acemoglu 10.1257/jep.33.2.3) come back as a ~25K-char Sci-Hub HTML
+    viewer page that passes any length threshold but is useless for M-58
+    extraction. Inspects the head of the content for HTML structural
+    markers or Sci-Hub branding (case-insensitive)."""
+    head = text[:600].lower()
+    return (
+        "<!doctype" in head
+        or "<html" in head
+        or "<head>" in head
+        or "<head " in head
+        or "<body" in head
+        or "sci-hub" in head
+    )
+
+
+def _is_usable_full_text(text: str | None) -> bool:
+    """A fetched OA full text is usable as the rich `direct_quote` source
+    only if it is SUBSTANTIAL (>= _OA_FULLTEXT_MIN_CHARS) AND clean prose
+    (not HTML / Sci-Hub junk). Otherwise the abstract fallbacks
+    (CrossRef / OpenAlex / PubMed) must take over (#1034)."""
+    return bool(
+        text
+        and len(text) >= _OA_FULLTEXT_MIN_CHARS
+        and not _looks_like_html_junk(text)
+    )
+

  781: def _looks_like_html_junk(text: str) -> bool:
  782:     """True when a fetched 'full text' is actually raw HTML markup or a
  783:     Sci-Hub wrapper page rather than clean extracted prose (#1034
  784:     follow-up). Ground-truthed: aeaweb paywalled econ papers (e.g.
  785:     Acemoglu 10.1257/jep.33.2.3) come back as a ~25K-char Sci-Hub HTML
  786:     viewer page that passes any length threshold but is useless for M-58
  787:     extraction. Inspects the head of the content for HTML structural
  788:     markers or Sci-Hub branding (case-insensitive)."""
  789:     head = text[:600].lower()
  790:     return (
  791:         "<!doctype" in head
  792:         or "<html" in head
  793:         or "<head>" in head
  794:         or "<head " in head
  795:         or "<body" in head
  796:         or "sci-hub" in head
  797:     )
  798: 
  799: 
  800: def _is_usable_full_text(text: str | None) -> bool:
  801:     """A fetched OA full text is usable as the rich `direct_quote` source
  802:     only if it is SUBSTANTIAL (>= _OA_FULLTEXT_MIN_CHARS) AND clean prose
  803:     (not HTML / Sci-Hub junk). Otherwise the abstract fallbacks
  804:     (CrossRef / OpenAlex / PubMed) must take over (#1034)."""
  805:     return bool(
  806:         text
  807:         and len(text) >= _OA_FULLTEXT_MIN_CHARS
  808:         and not _looks_like_html_junk(text)
  809:     )

  811: 
  812: def _pick_richest_abstract(
  813:     *,
  814:     crossref: str | None,
  815:     openalex: str | None,
  816:     pubmed: str | None,
  817:     partial_full_text: str | None = None,
  818: ) -> tuple[str, str]:
  819:     """Choose the RICHEST (longest) available abstract text + its
  820:     quote_source label. Candidates in priority order CrossRef >
  821:     OpenAlex > PubMed > thin-OA-full-text partial; the LONGEST wins,
  822:     ties break toward the higher-priority source (deterministic —
  823:     strictly-greater comparison while iterating priority order).
  824: 
  825:     A thin oa_full_text stub (paywalled-PDF Jina result, ~540 chars)
  826:     is admitted only as the last-priority `partial_full_text`
  827:     candidate, so a real abstract (e.g. OpenAlex 1331 chars) overrides
  828:     it rather than being blocked by it (issue #1034). Returns
  829:     ("", "none") when every candidate is empty."""
  830:     candidates: list[tuple[str, str]] = []
  831:     if crossref:
  832:         candidates.append((crossref, "crossref_abstract"))
  833:     if openalex:
  834:         candidates.append((openalex, "openalex_abstract"))
  835:     if pubmed:
  836:         candidates.append((pubmed, "pubmed_abstract"))
  837:     # A thin OA full-text stub is a TRUE last resort: admit it ONLY when
  838:     # no real abstract resolved. Per §-1.1 clinical-safety (dual-audit
  839:     # finding #1034), a paywall junk stub must never become the extracted
  840:     # span when a real abstract exists — even if the stub is longer.
  841:     if partial_full_text and not candidates:
  842:         candidates.append((partial_full_text, "oa_full_text_partial"))
  843:     best: tuple[str, str] | None = None
  844:     for text, src in candidates:
  845:         if best is None or len(text) > len(best[0]):
  846:             best = (text, src)
  847:     return best if best is not None else ("", "none")
  848:

  936:         # FIX-D5: Retry once on timeout errors before giving up
  937:         if timeout_occurred:
  938:             logger.info("[ACCESS] Retrying direct fetch after timeout for %s", url[:60])
  939:             await asyncio.sleep(3)
  940:             retry_result = await self._direct_fetch(url)
  941:             if retry_result.success:
  942:                 # M-23b: strip BEFORE paywall detection
  943:                 retry_result.content = _strip_navigation_boilerplate(retry_result.content)
  944:                 if not self._detect_paywall(retry_result.content):
  945:                     return retry_result
  946: 
  947:         # PL: Sci-Hub fallback for paywalled academic papers (last resort)
  948:         # Use resolved DOI if available (more reliable than URL-based DOI extraction)
  949:         if os.getenv("PG_SCIHUB_ENABLED", "1") == "1":
  950:             scihub_url = url
  951:             if resolved_doi:
  952:                 scihub_url = f"https://doi.org/{resolved_doi}"
  953:             scihub_result = await self._try_scihub(scihub_url)
  954:             if scihub_result.success:
  955:                 logger.info("[ACCESS] Sci-Hub succeeded for %s (%d chars)", url[:60], len(scihub_result.content))
  956:                 scihub_result.content = _strip_navigation_boilerplate(scihub_result.content)
  957:                 return scihub_result
  958: 
  959:         # SF-40: Log total failure at WARNING (was completely silent)
  960:         logger.warning("[ACCESS] ALL access methods exhausted for %s", url[:80])
  961:         return AccessResult(
  962:             url=url,
  963:             content="",
  964:             access_method="failed",
  965:             legal_alternative=None,
  966:             success=False,
  967:             metadata={"error": "All access methods failed"}
  968:         )
  969: 
  970:     async def _try_crawl4ai(self, url: str) -> AccessResult:
 2270:                 art_match = re.search(r"articles/(s\d+-\d+-\d+-\w+)", url)
 2271:                 if art_match:
 2272:                     doi = f"10.1038/{art_match.group(1)}"
 2273: 
 2274:         return resolved_url or url, doi
 2275: 
 2276:     async def _try_scihub(self, url: str) -> AccessResult:
 2277:         """PL: Try Sci-Hub for paywalled academic papers.
 2278: 
 2279:         Extracts DOI from URL, queries Sci-Hub mirrors, downloads PDF,
 2280:         and converts to text via PyMuPDF. Last resort after all legal
 2281:         methods exhausted.
 2282:         """
 2283:         import aiohttp
 2284:         import re
 2285: 
 2286:         # Extract DOI from URL
 2287:         doi = None
 2288:         doi_match = re.search(r"(10\.\d{4,9}/[^\s\])<>\"',;]+)", url)
 2289:         if doi_match:
 2290:             doi = doi_match.group(1).rstrip(".")
 2291: 
 2292:         if not doi:
 2293:             return AccessResult(url=url, content="", access_method="scihub",
 2294:                                 legal_alternative=None, success=False,
 2295:                                 metadata={"error": "No DOI found in URL"})
 2296: 
 2297:         mirrors = ["https://sci-hub.st", "https://sci-hub.ru"]
 2298:         timeout = aiohttp.ClientTimeout(total=20)
 2299: 
 2300:         for mirror in mirrors:
 2301:             try:
 2302:                 async with aiohttp.ClientSession(timeout=timeout) as session:
 2303:                     scihub_url = f"{mirror}/{doi}"
 2304:                     async with session.get(scihub_url) as resp:
 2305:                         if resp.status != 200:
 2306:                             continue
 2307:                         html = await resp.text()
 2308: 
 2309:                         # Check if paper is available
 2310:                         if "not available" in html.lower()[:500]:
 2311:                             continue
 2312: 
 2313:                         # Extract PDF URL from embed/iframe
 2314:                         pdf_match = re.search(
 2315:                             r'(?:embed|iframe)[^>]+src=["\']([^"\']+\.pdf[^"\']*)',
 2316:                             html,
 2317:                         )
 2318:                         if not pdf_match:
 2319:                             # Try direct PDF link pattern
 2320:                             pdf_match = re.search(r'(//[^\s"<>]+\.pdf)', html)
 2321: 
 2322:                         if not pdf_match:
 2323:                             # No PDF found but page loaded — try extracting
 2324:                             # text content from the HTML itself
 2325:                             if len(html) > 5000:
 2326:                                 return AccessResult(
 2327:                                     url=url, content=html[:30000],
 2328:                                     access_method="scihub_html",
 2329:                                     legal_alternative=scihub_url,
 2330:                                     success=True,
 2331:                                     metadata={"doi": doi, "mirror": mirror},
 2332:                                 )
 2333:                             continue
 2334: 
 2335:                         pdf_url = pdf_match.group(1)
 2336:                         if pdf_url.startswith("//"):
 2337:                             pdf_url = "https:" + pdf_url
 2338: 
 2339:                         # Download PDF
 2340:                         async with session.get(pdf_url) as pdf_resp:
 2341:                             if pdf_resp.status != 200:
 2342:                                 continue
 2343:                             pdf_bytes = await pdf_resp.read()
 2344: 
 2345:                         # Extract text from PDF
 2346:                         try:
 2347:                             import fitz  # PyMuPDF
 2348:                             doc = fitz.open(stream=pdf_bytes, filetype="pdf")
 2349:                             text_parts = []
 2350:                             for page in doc:
 2351:                                 text_parts.append(page.get_text())
 2352:                             doc.close()
 2353:                             full_text = "\n\n".join(text_parts)
 2354: 
 2355:                             if len(full_text) > 500:
 2356:                                 logger.info(
 2357:                                     "[ACCESS] Sci-Hub PDF extracted for %s: %d chars from %d pages",
 2358:                                     doi, len(full_text), len(text_parts),
 2359:                                 )
 2360:                                 return AccessResult(
 2361:                                     url=url, content=full_text[:50000],
 2362:                                     access_method="scihub_pdf",
 2363:                                     legal_alternative=scihub_url,
 2364:                                     success=True,
 2365:                                     metadata={"doi": doi, "mirror": mirror, "pages": len(text_parts)},
 2366:                                 )
 2367:                         except ImportError:
 2368:                             logger.warning("[ACCESS] PyMuPDF not installed — cannot extract Sci-Hub PDF")
 2369:                         except Exception as pdf_exc:
 2370:                             logger.warning("[ACCESS] Sci-Hub PDF extraction failed: %s", str(pdf_exc)[:100])
 2371: 
 2372:             except Exception as exc:
 2373:                 logger.debug("[ACCESS] Sci-Hub mirror %s failed: %s", mirror, str(exc)[:80])
 2374: 
 2375:         return AccessResult(url=url, content="", access_method="scihub",
 2376:                             legal_alternative=None, success=False,
 2377:                             metadata={"error": "All Sci-Hub mirrors failed", "doi": doi})

 succeeded in 965ms:
  860: # stack (Crawl4AI + Jina Reader + Firecrawl concurrent) used
  861: # elsewhere for content extraction. Used by M-56 for:
  862: #
  863: #   - M-66b-R: url_pattern-primary regulatory entities (FDA, EMA,
  864: #     NICE, HC landing pages) where no DOI/PMID exists.
  865: #   - M-66b-T: OA PDF/HTML full-text fetch when Unpaywall
  866: #     surfaced an OA URL — upgrades direct_quote from abstract
  867: #     to full text so M-58 can extract 9-field SURPASS rosters.
  868: #
  869: # Returns `(content_str, final_url_str)` on success, `("", "")` on
  870: # failure. Caller decides provenance class + attempt logging.
  871: # Content is truncated at `_M66_CONTENT_CAP` chars for prompt-
  872: # budget predictability.
  873: _M66_CONTENT_CAP = 25000
  874: 
  875: 
  876: def _fetch_url_pattern(url: str) -> tuple[str, str]:
  877:     """Fetch content at `url` via AccessBypass. Returns
  878:     `(content, final_url)` or `("", "")` on failure.
  879: 
  880:     Deterministic-test seam: this function is the mockable
  881:     boundary for M-66b-R / M-66b-T tests (stub via
  882:     `monkeypatch.setattr("...frame_fetcher._fetch_url_pattern",
  883:     lambda u: ("stubbed content", u))`).
  884: 
  885:     AccessBypass.fetch_with_bypass is async; M-56 is sync. The
  886:     helper wraps the async call in asyncio.run(). If an event
  887:     loop is already running in the caller's thread (live server
  888:     context), we fall back to a fresh thread + new loop so this
  889:     helper is safe to invoke from any caller context.
  890:     """
  891:     if not url:
  892:         return "", ""
  893:     try:
  894:         import asyncio as _asyncio
  895:         from src.tools.access_bypass import AccessBypass
  896: 
  897:         async def _run() -> tuple[str, str]:
  898:             ab = AccessBypass()
  899:             result = await ab.fetch_with_bypass(url)
  900:             if result is None or not getattr(result, "success", False):
  901:                 return "", ""
  902:             content = getattr(result, "content", "") or ""
  903:             final_url = getattr(result, "url", "") or url
  904:             if not content:
  905:                 return "", ""
  906:             return content[:_M66_CONTENT_CAP], final_url
  907: 
  908:         try:
  909:             # Probe for a running loop. asyncio.get_running_loop
  910:             # raises RuntimeError when no loop is running (normal
  911:             # sync context); the no-warning way to ask.
  912:             _asyncio.get_running_loop()
  913:             # A loop IS running — spin a fresh one in a worker
  914:             # thread so we don't collide with it (e.g. live-server
  915:             # FastAPI context).
  916:             import concurrent.futures as _cf
  917: 
  918:             def _thread_run() -> tuple[str, str]:

  952:     Returns:
  953:         FrameRow — always non-None. A FRAME_GAP_UNRECOVERABLE row is
  954:         still a valid return — callers inspect `is_gap()` or
  955:         `provenance_class` to branch.

  957:     Deterministic per design — same (binding, upstream API state) →

  967:             client.close()

    5: `FourRoleEvaluationInputs` bundle that the sweep hands to
    6: `run_four_role_evaluation` (sweep_integration.py). It does NO file I/O: it RETURNS a
    7: `NativeGateBBundle` (inputs + audit_map); M3b is responsible for writing
    8: `four_role_claim_audit.json` next to the run (Codex P2 #2).
    9: 
   10: CONTAMINATION-CRITICAL (§-1.1 LETHAL otherwise — operator-locked, NOT consultable):
   11: This module builds every input ONLY from NATIVE config — the scope template's
   12: `per_query_report_contract[<slug>].required_entities` and the D8 release-policy config
   13: (`d8_config.s0_must_cover_categories`). It MUST NEVER import or read anything under
   14: `outputs/dr_benchmark/` (gold rubric / freeze pin / competitor answers). The required-
   15: element denominator, the claim->element coverage map, and per-claim severity all come
   16: from native pre-registered annotations — never from the benchmark gold rubric.
   17: 
   18: Canonical-identifier note (Codex P2 #4): the frozen `EvidenceDocument`
   19: (`role_transport.py`) carries only `doc_id` + `text`. The CANONICAL identifiers used for
   20: coverage (DOI / PMID / full canonical URL) therefore come from the `evidence_lookup`
   21: RECORD keyed by evidence_id. The builder's record contract is `{text, doi?, pmid?, url?}`;
   22: M3b NORMALIZES each raw `evidence_pool.json` row (which carries `source_url` and embeds a
   23: DOI) into that `{doi, pmid, url}` shape before calling this builder. The native scope ENTITY
   24: declares its URL identity under `url_pattern` (clinical.yaml regulatory entities) and its
   25: trial identity under `doi`/`pmid`. Coverage is EXACT EQUALITY per (entity-key, record-key)
   26: pair — never substring/`in`/`startswith` — so a broad `url_pattern` FRAGMENT can never `==`
   27: a full resolved URL and thus fails closed (P2 #4). The URL pair is ASYMMETRIC: entity
   28: `url_pattern` vs record `url`.

   78: # --- evidence-record normalization (M3b; LOAD-BEARING, deterministic, NO network) ---------
   79: # The raw evidence_pool.json row carries `source_url` + the evidence text under `direct_quote`
   80: # (the field strict_verify's ProvenanceToken spans index into — see provenance_generator.py)

   85: _RAW_TEXT_KEYS = ("direct_quote", "statement", "text")

   87: # Deterministic DOI: the canonical `10.<registrant>/<suffix>` form (CrossRef pattern).
   88: _DOI_RE = re.compile(r"10\.\d{4,9}/[-._;()/:A-Za-z0-9]+")
   89: # Publisher URL path-suffixes appended AFTER the DOI in a landing-page URL (e.g.
   90: # frontiersin.org/.../10.3389/fphar.2022.1016639/full). Trimmed so the extracted DOI is the
   91: # bare canonical token that EXACTLY equals the entity's `doi` (P2 #4). Order matters: longest
   92: # first. Trailing punctuation (a `.` or `;` lifted from prose) is also stripped.
   93: _DOI_URL_SUFFIXES = ("/full", "/abstract", "/pdf", "/meta", "/html", "/epdf")
   94: _DOI_TRAILING_PUNCT = ".,;)"
   95: # Deterministic PMID: a PubMed URL path id (`pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/<id>` or `/pubmed/<id>`)
   96: # or an explicit `PMID: <id>` token. Bare numeric so it `==` the entity's `pmid` (int -> str).
   97: _PMID_URL_RE = re.compile(r"(?:ncbi\.nlm\.nih\.gov/(?:pubmed|m/pubmed)?/?|/pubmed/)(\d+)")
   98: _PMID_TOKEN_RE = re.compile(r"\bPMID:?\s*(\d+)", re.IGNORECASE)

  107:     verbatim to `run_four_role_evaluation`.

  114: def _normalize_sentence(sentence: str) -> str:
  115:     """Lowercase + collapse whitespace (the basis for the deterministic claim_id hash)."""
  116:     return _WHITESPACE_RE.sub(" ", sentence.lower()).strip()
  117: 
  118: 
  119: def _row_text(row: Mapping[str, Any]) -> str:
  120:     """The evidence text the strict_verify spans were validated against (first non-empty).
  121: 
  122:     Prefers `direct_quote` (the field ProvenanceToken char-spans index into), then `statement`,
  123:     then `text`. Empty text is NOT raised here — the builder's `_resolve_evidence` fails closed
  124:     on empty text at claim-resolution time (so an evidence row never cited stays harmless).
  125:     """
  126:     for key in _RAW_TEXT_KEYS:

**Findings**
- P1: `PG_FRAME_PREFER_ABSTRACT` does not actually bypass the scrape. [frame_fetcher.py](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/frame_fetcher.py:1117) still calls `_fetch_url_pattern()` before the abstract decision, so the run can still hit non-deterministic `access_bypass` and Sci-Hub even when the final `direct_quote` is abstract.
- P1: Sci-Hub PDF text can still be laundered as `oa_full_text`. [access_bypass.py](C:/POLARIS/src/tools/access_bypass.py:949) enables Sci-Hub by default, [access_bypass.py](C:/POLARIS/src/tools/access_bypass.py:2360) returns clean `scihub_pdf` text, and [frame_fetcher.py](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/frame_fetcher.py:897) drops the access method. `_looks_like_html_junk` catches Sci-Hub HTML, not Sci-Hub PDF provenance.
- P2: `_looks_like_html_junk` is good for the observed HTML case, but misses non-HTML junk like Jina landing markdown. Under flag-off, or flag-on with no abstract, that can still become `direct_quote`.
- P2: `OPEN_ACCESS` remains semantically overloaded when `quote_source` is `crossref_abstract`/`openalex_abstract`; the enum doc says it means full OA text was captured.

The design call is right: for Gate-B frame-contract fields that are abstract-level, preferring the stable abstract over a noisy scrape is the correct grounding choice, and default-off protects the clinical full-text roster path. `_pick_richest_abstract` tie-handling is deterministic.

Verification: focused tests passed: `TestHtmlJunkAndPreferAbstract`, `TestOpenAlexThinStubRichest`, and related `-k` selection. Full `test_m56_frame_fetcher.py` timed out after 5 minutes with the completed prefix green.

**Findings**
- P1: `PG_FRAME_PREFER_ABSTRACT` does not actually bypass the scrape. [frame_fetcher.py](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/frame_fetcher.py:1117) still calls `_fetch_url_pattern()` before the abstract decision, so the run can still hit non-deterministic `access_bypass` and Sci-Hub even when the final `direct_quote` is abstract.
- P1: Sci-Hub PDF text can still be laundered as `oa_full_text`. [access_bypass.py](C:/POLARIS/src/tools/access_bypass.py:949) enables Sci-Hub by default, [access_bypass.py](C:/POLARIS/src/tools/access_bypass.py:2360) returns clean `scihub_pdf` text, and [frame_fetcher.py](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/frame_fetcher.py:897) drops the access method. `_looks_like_html_junk` catches Sci-Hub HTML, not Sci-Hub PDF provenance.
- P2: `_looks_like_html_junk` is good for the observed HTML case, but misses non-HTML junk like Jina landing markdown. Under flag-off, or flag-on with no abstract, that can still become `direct_quote`.
- P2: `OPEN_ACCESS` remains semantically overloaded when `quote_source` is `crossref_abstract`/`openalex_abstract`; the enum doc says it means full OA text was captured.

The design call is right: for Gate-B frame-contract fields that are abstract-level, preferring the stable abstract over a noisy scrape is the correct grounding choice, and default-off protects the clinical full-text roster path. `_pick_richest_abstract` tie-handling is deterministic.
